<h1 class="c-article-title" itemprop="headline">Gaddafi’s son offers to give evidence that Libya funded Sarkozy election bid</h1>

            <div class="c-article-meta-container ">
              <div class="c-article-meta">

    <h5 itemprop="author"

          </span>

Euronews that Libya funded the former French president\u2019s 2007 election bid.&quot;,&quot;keySentence&quot;:null,&quot;url&quot;:&quot;gaddafi-s-son-offers-to-give-evidence-that-libya-funded-sarkozy-election-bid&quot;,&quot;masterCms&quot;:&quot;v2&quot;,&quot;plainText&quot;:&quot;The son of the deposed Libyan leader Muammar Gaddafi has welcomed the detention of Nicolas Sarkozy and repeated his offer to provide evidence that the former French president\u2019s 2007 election campaign was funded illicitly by the Libyan government. \n\nSaif al-Islam \u2013 who made the allegations in an  exclusive interview with Euronews in 2011  \u2013 told our sister channel  Africanews  that he regretted it had taken the French authorities seven years to act. \n\nIn a series of messages sent by WhatsApp, Gaddafi\u2019s son claimed he had witnessed the first portion of money being delivered in Tripoli to Sarkozy\u2019s former chief-of-staff Claude Gu\u00e9ant. \n\nHe added that he was one of several witnesses who were ready to testify \u2013 including Abdallah Snoussi, ex-director of the Libyan intelligence services, and Bashir Salah, former chief executive of Libya Investment. \n\nSnoussi has a recording of the first meeting between Sarkozy and Gaddafi in Tripoli before his 2007 election campaign, al-Islam claims. He alleges that both men made a second delivery of cash to Paris. \n\nNicolas Sarkozy \u2013 who was President of France from 2007 until 2012 \u2013 has been  questioned for a second day  by police near Paris. Investigations were prompted by the French news website Mediapart\u2019s publication of accusations made by a Franco-Lebanese businessman, Ziad Takieddine, who said he transferred \u20ac5 million to Gu\u00e9ant from Gaddafi\u2019s former intelligence chief. \n\nThere has been no comment from Sarkozy or his lawyers since the 63-year-old was  taken into custody on Tuesday . In the past the ex-president has dismissed the accusations as \u201cgrotesque\u201d and a \u201cmanipulation\u201d. His party, Les R\u00e9publicains, have said they fully support their former leader.   \n\nTakieddine has been quoted by a Lebanese newspaper as saying he acted as an intermediary between France and Libya when Sarkozy was interior minister, before his presidential bid. Five months after his election, Gaddafi came to Paris on his first state visit to a Western country in decades. \n\nHowever, by 2011 the then French president had turned against the Libyan leader. France was at the forefront of NATO-led airstrikes against Gaddafi\u2019s forces that helped rebel fighters overthrow the dictator and his regime. \n\nIt was around this time that Gaddafi\u2019s son, Saif al-Islam, made his comments to Euronews as he expressed outrage at France\u2019s recognition of the rebel groups\u2019 interim government set up in Benghazi.&quot;,&quot;htmlText&quot;:{&quot;first&quot;:&quot;&lt;p&gt;The son of the deposed Libyan leader Muammar Gaddafi has welcomed the detention of Nicolas Sarkozy and repeated his offer to provide evidence that the former French president\u2019s 2007 election campaign was funded illicitly by the Libyan government.&lt;\/p&gt;&quot;,&quot;second&quot;:&quot;\n&lt;p&gt;Saif al-Islam \u2013 who made the allegations in an &lt;a href=\&quot;http:\/\/www.euronews.com\/2011\/03\/16\/gaddafi-s-son-calls-the-libyan-rebels-traitors\&quot;&gt;exclusive interview with Euronews in 2011&lt;\/a&gt; \u2013 told our sister channel &lt;a href=\&quot;http:\/\/www.africanews.com\/2018\/03\/20\/gaddafi-s-son-saif-al-islam-welcomes-sarkozy-arrest-offers-evidence\/\&quot;&gt;Africanews&lt;\/a&gt; that he regretted it had taken the French authorities seven years to act.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;In a series of messages sent by WhatsApp, Gaddafi\u2019s son claimed he had witnessed the first portion of money being delivered in Tripoli to Sarkozy\u2019s former chief-of-staff Claude Gu\u00e9ant.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;He added that he was one of several witnesses who were ready to testify \u2013 including Abdallah Snoussi, ex-director of the Libyan intelligence services, and Bashir Salah, former chief executive of Libya Investment.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Snoussi has a recording of the first meeting between Sarkozy and Gaddafi in Tripoli before his 2007 election campaign, al-Islam claims. He alleges that both men made a second delivery of cash to Paris.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Nicolas Sarkozy \u2013 who was President of France from 2007 until 2012 \u2013 has been &lt;a href=\&quot;http:\/\/www.euronews.com\/2018\/03\/21\/sarkozy-questioned-a-second-day-over-allegations-of-libyan-funding\&quot;&gt;questioned for a second day&lt;\/a&gt; by police near Paris. Investigations were prompted by the French news website Mediapart\u2019s publication of accusations made by a Franco-Lebanese businessman, Ziad Takieddine, who said he transferred \u20ac5 million to Gu\u00e9ant from Gaddafi\u2019s former intelligence chief.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;There has been no comment from Sarkozy or his lawyers since the 63-year-old was &lt;a href=\&quot;http:\/\/www.euronews.com\/2018\/03\/20\/ex-french-president-sarkozy-custody-over-alleged-gadhafi-links-source-n858141\&quot;&gt;taken into custody on Tuesday&lt;\/a&gt;. In the past the ex-president has dismissed the accusations as \u201cgrotesque\u201d and a \u201cmanipulation\u201d. His party, Les R\u00e9publicains, have said they fully support their former leader.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;Takieddine has been quoted by a Lebanese newspaper as saying he acted as an intermediary between France and Libya when Sarkozy was interior minister, before his presidential bid. Five months after his election, Gaddafi came to Paris on his first state visit to a Western country in decades.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;However, by 2011 the then French president had turned against the Libyan leader. France was at the forefront of NATO-led airstrikes against Gaddafi\u2019s forces that helped rebel fighters overthrow the dictator and his regime.&lt;\/p&gt;\n&lt;p&gt;It was around this time that Gaddafi\u2019s son, Saif al-Islam, made his comments to Euronews as he expressed outrage at France\u2019s recognition of the rebel groups\u2019 interim government set up in             <div class="column small-12 medium-10 xlarge-11 js-responsive-iframes-container">
                              <div class="c-font-size-switcher medium-order-4 js-font-size-switch u-float-end u-padding-top-0 t-font-size-switcher--blue">
        <span class="c-font-size-switcher__text text-center">Text size</span>
      <a href="#" class="c-font-size-switcher__link-small js-font-size-switch-small current-font-size">
    Aa
  </a>
  <a href="#" class="c-font-size-switcher__link-big js-font-size-switch-big">
    Aa
  </a>
</div>


                              <div class="c-article-content  js-article-content article__content"
       itemprop="articleBody">
    <div class="c-article-content__first-element"></div>
    <p>The son of the deposed Libyan leader Muammar Gaddafi has welcomed the detention of Nicolas Sarkozy and repeated his offer to provide evidence that the former French president’s 2007 election campaign was funded illicitly by the Libyan government.</p>
  </div>

      <div class="show-for-small-only ">
      <div class="enw-MPU ">
  <div id="adzone-mpu_1" class="enw-MPU__img advertising"></div>
</div>



    </div>
    <div class="c-article-content  js-article-content article__content"
       itemprop="articleBody">
    
<p>Saif al-Islam – who made the allegations in an <a href="http://www.euronews.com/2011/03/16/gaddafi-s-son-calls-the-libyan-rebels-traitors">exclusive interview with Euronews in 2011</a> – told our sister channel <a href="http://www.africanews.com/2018/03/20/gaddafi-s-son-saif-al-islam-welcomes-sarkozy-arrest-offers-evidence/">Africanews</a> that he regretted it had taken the French authorities seven years to act.</p>
<p>In a series of messages sent by WhatsApp, Gaddafi’s son claimed he had witnessed the first portion of money being delivered in Tripoli to Sarkozy’s former chief-of-staff Claude Guéant.</p>
<p>He added that he was one of several witnesses who were ready to testify – including Abdallah Snoussi, ex-director of the Libyan intelligence services, and Bashir Salah, former chief executive of Libya Investment.</p>
<p>Snoussi has a recording of the first meeting between Sarkozy and Gaddafi in Tripoli before his 2007 election campaign, al-Islam claims. He alleges that both men made a second delivery of cash to Paris.</p>
<p>Nicolas Sarkozy – who was President of France from 2007 until 2012 – has been <a href="http://www.euronews.com/2018/03/21/sarkozy-questioned-a-second-day-over-allegations-of-libyan-funding">questioned for a second day</a> by police near Paris. Investigations were prompted by the French news website Mediapart’s publication of accusations made by a Franco-Lebanese businessman, Ziad Takieddine, who said he transferred €5 million to Guéant from Gaddafi’s former intelligence chief.</p>
<p>There has been no comment from Sarkozy or his lawyers since the 63-year-old was <a href="http://www.euronews.com/2018/03/20/ex-french-president-sarkozy-custody-over-alleged-gadhafi-links-source-n858141">taken into custody on Tuesday</a>. In the past the ex-president has dismissed the accusations as “grotesque” and a “manipulation”. His party, Les Républicains, have said they fully support their former leader.</p>
<p>Takieddine has been quoted by a Lebanese newspaper as saying he acted as an intermediary between France and Libya when Sarkozy was interior minister, before his presidential bid. Five months after his election, Gaddafi came to Paris on his first state visit to a Western country in decades.</p>
<p>However, by 2011 the then French president had turned against the Libyan leader. France was at the forefront of NATO-led airstrikes against Gaddafi’s forces that helped rebel fighters overthrow the dictator and his regime.</p>
<p>It was around this time that Gaddafi’s son, Saif al-Islam, made his comments to Euronews as he expressed outrage at France’s recognition of the rebel groups’ interim government set up in Benghazi.</p>
<p><div class="widget widget--type-freeform
widget--size-fullwidth
widget--align-center">
  <div class="widget__wrapper">
    <div class="widget__ratio widget__ratio--auto">

      </div>
    </div>
  </div>
</div>
</p>

  </div>
